## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**29 key C++ symbols** representing the core architectural components including filter types, factory interfaces, and management classes.

**The execution chain** showing how filters are created and executed:
1. New stream arrives → ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()
2. FilterManager created and initialized
3. FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain() invoked
4. FilterChainUtility instantiates each filter via factory callbacks
5. Per-request filter execution through decoder/encoder phases

Envoy is built on a factory-based architecture distributed across multiple C++ files. Here is how the key components work together:\\n\\n## Core Architecture\\n\\n**Filter Interfaces (envoy/http/filter.h):** Defines the base filter types (StreamFilter, StreamDecoderFilter, StreamEncoderFilter) and the status enums (FilterHeadersStatus, FilterDataStatus, FilterTrailersStatus) that control filter chain iteration.\\n\\n**Filter Factory (envoy/http/filter_factory.h):** Defines the factory pattern with FilterFactoryCb (a callback that creates filters), FilterChainFactory (creates filter chains for new streams), FilterChainManager (manages filter instantiation), and FilterChainOptions (provides filter configuration options like disabling filters per-route).\\n\\n**Filter Configuration (envoy/server/filter_config.h):** Defines HttpFilterConfigFactoryBase, NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory, and UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory - these are the registry points where filter implementations register their factories.\\n\\n## Filter Chain Creation\\n\\n**HTTP Connection Manager (source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.h):** The HttpConnectionManagerConfig implements FilterChainFactory and drives filter chain creation through its createFilterChain() method. This is invoked for each new HTTP stream.\\n\\n**Filter Chain Utility (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h):** FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories() is the central function that iterates through registered filter factories and calls applyFilterFactoryCb on each to instantiate filters. It also handles filter dependencies validation.\\n\\n## Per-Request Filter Chain Execution\\n\\n**Connection Manager Stream Creation (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h):** When ConnectionManagerImpl receives a new HTTP stream via newStream(), it creates an ActiveStream and instantiates a FilterManager.\\n\\n**Filter Manager (source/common/http/filter_manager.h):** The FilterManager (specifically DownstreamFilterManager for downstream streams) orchestrates the entire filter chain lifecycle:\\n- Maintains separate lists of decoder_filters_ and encoder_filters_ (stored as ActiveStreamDecoderFilter and ActiveStreamEncoderFilter)\\n- Implements the filter iteration logic in decodeHeaders(), decodeData(), decodeTrailers(), encodeHeaders(), encodeData(), encodeTrailers() methods\\n- Respects FilterHeadersStatus/FilterDataStatus return codes to control iteration (Continue, StopIteration, StopAllIterationAndBuffer)\\n- Manages filter context and invokes filters in order\\n\\n**Filter Callbacks (source/common/http/filter_manager.h):** FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl implements FilterChainFactoryCallbacks and is called during filter chain creation. Its addStreamDecoderFilter(), addStreamEncoderFilter(), and addStreamFilter() methods wrap the raw filter pointers in ActiveStreamDecoderFilter/ActiveStreamEncoderFilter and add them to the manager's filter lists.\\n\\n**Active Stream Filters (source/common/http/filter_manager.h):** ActiveStreamDecoderFilter and ActiveStreamEncoderFilter wrap individual filter instances and inherit from ActiveStreamFilterBase, which provides the base behavior for state tracking, iteration control, and callbacks. These objects are instantiated once per filter per stream and hold the filter instance.\\n\\n## Dependency Management\\n\\n**Dependency Manager (source/common/http/dependency_manager.h):** Validates HTTP filter chain dependencies declared in filter factories to ensure filters are ordered correctly (e.g., router filter must be last).\\n\\n**Dynamic Filter Configuration (source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h):** HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl supports dynamic filter configuration for both downstream and upstream filters.\\n\\n## Key Data Flow\\n\\nFor each new HTTP request:\\n1. ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream() is called\\n2. DownstreamFilterManager is created with reference to FilterChainFactory\\n3. FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain() is invoked, which calls FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()\\n4. Each filter factory's FilterFactoryCb is called with FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl\\n5. Filters call addStreamDecoderFilter/addStreamEncoderFilter, which creates ActiveStreamXxxFilter wrappers\\n6. When data arrives, FilterManager::decodeHeaders/decodeData/etc invoke filters in order\\n7. Each filter's return status controls whether iteration continues or stops\\n8. Response data flows through encoder filters in reverse order\"\n}\n",

It also handles filter dependencies validation.\\n\\n## Per-Request Filter Chain Execution\\n\\n**Connection Manager Stream Creation (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h):** When ConnectionManagerImpl receives a new HTTP stream via newStream(), it creates an ActiveStream and instantiates a FilterManager.\\n\\n**Filter Manager (source/common/http/filter_manager.h):** The FilterManager (specifically DownstreamFilterManager for downstream streams) orchestrates the entire filter chain lifecycle:\\n- Maintains separate lists of decoder_filters_ and encoder_filters_ (stored as ActiveStreamDecoderFilter and ActiveStreamEncoderFilter)\\n- Implements the filter iteration logic in decodeHeaders(), decodeData(), decodeTrailers(), encodeHeaders(), encodeData(), encodeTrailers() methods\\n- Respects FilterHeadersStatus/FilterDataStatus return codes to control iteration (Continue, StopIteration, StopAllIterationAndBuffer)\\n- Manages filter context and invokes filters in order\\n\\n**Filter Callbacks (source/common/http/filter_manager.h):** FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl implements FilterChainFactoryCallbacks and is called during filter chain creation. Its addStreamDecoderFilter(), addStreamEncoderFilter(), and addStreamFilter() methods wrap the raw filter pointers in ActiveStreamDecoderFilter/ActiveStreamEncoderFilter and add them to the manager's filter lists.\\n\\n**Active Stream Filters (source/common/http/filter_manager.h):** ActiveStreamDecoderFilter and ActiveStreamEncoderFilter wrap individual filter instances and inherit from ActiveStreamFilterBase, which provides the base behavior for state tracking, iteration control, and callbacks. These objects are instantiated once per filter per stream and hold the filter instance.\\n\\n## Dependency Management\\n\\n**Dependency Manager (source/common/http/dependency_manager.h):** Validates HTTP filter chain dependencies declared in filter factories to ensure filters are ordered correctly (e.g., router filter must be last).\\n\\n**Dynamic Filter Configuration (source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h):** HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl supports dynamic filter configuration for both downstream and upstream filters.\\n\\n## Key Data Flow\\n\\nFor each new HTTP request:\\n1. ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream() is called\\n2. DownstreamFilterManager is created with reference to FilterChainFactory\\n3. FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain() is invoked, which calls FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()\\n4. Each filter factory's FilterFactoryCb is called with FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl\\n5. Filters call addStreamDecoderFilter/addStreamEncoderFilter, which creates ActiveStreamXxxFilter wrappers\\n6. When data arrives, FilterManager::decodeHeaders/decodeData/etc invoke filters in order\\n7. Each filter's return status controls whether iteration continues or stops\\n8. Response data flows through encoder filters in reverse order\"\n}\n",
